Kesari\n\\\nAssistant Professor \\\nof Engineering\n\end{flushright}%\n}\n~~\n\parbox[c][1in][t]{6cm}{\n\begin{flushleft}\n School of Engineering\n \\\n  Brown University\n \\\n  182 Hope Street, B\&H 735\n \\\n Providence, RI 02912\n \\\n Phone: 401-863-1418\n \\\nEmail: Haneesh\_Kesari@brown.edu\n\end{flushleft}%\n}\n}\n}}\n\lthUiuc\n\n\n\n\n\n%\n%\n\namefrom{Haneesh Kesari}%\n\n\n\nameto{National Science Foundation}\n\addrto{\n\parbox{3.5in}%\n{\nGraduate Research Fellowship Program}%\n}\n\regarding{Tom Pilvelait Recommendation}%\n\greetto{To the Fellowship Selection Committee:}%\n\closeline{Sincerely,}%\n\n\begin{document}%\n\n\begin{newlfm}\n\nI would like to recommend my student Tom Pilvelait for the National Science Foundation Graduate Research Fellowship. Tom is a genuinely talented student who has shown great promise as a budding research scientist.  \n\nTom is currently a first year graduate student who has worked with me in the Applied Mechanics Lab at Brown since August 2019. Although I have only known Tom for a short amount of time, his research abilities seem quite strong. Recently, Tom has conducted various experimental studies into the dynamics of fracture in dry spaghetti and with this he has already shown great versatility in his research capabilities. This ranges from practical experimental techniques such as machine shop skills and building circuits to demonstrating quickness in understanding new theoretical concepts. At the start of the project, theories of fracture were entirely new to Tom, yet time and again he has proven highly enthusiastic in learning new concepts. It is for these reasons I have recommended that Tom submit an abstract to present our findings at the American Physical Society March Meeting in 2020 despite how recently he started at Brown. Indeed, this simple introductory research project will likely result in a publication in the near future.\n\nAs a recent example, Tom and I were interested in studying the mechanical properties of the spaghetti so as to develop a model of fracture in this system. There are, however, material and geometric limitations set by the spaghetti, which precludes one from testing the spaghetti in a standardized manner (e.g. via ASTM standards). Tom was able to develop rather creative solutions in testing the shear and tensile strength of the otherwise unwieldly spaghetti. Several long, substantive discussions on the issues associated with this testing has led us to discover a fundamental issue in the metrology of material properties, which may be publishable work in its own right.\n\nDespite this current project’s success, Tom and I originally connected over his and my research interests in frictional mechanics. His undergraduate research demonstrates a good level of preparedness in this field. As a result, his project proposal on “Developing a Mechanistic Model of Friction” is foundationally solid. His prior experience in experimental frictional mechanics allows him to be in a unique position for this project. Similar to his current work in the spaghetti fracture project, Tom seems to have a propensity for understanding foundational concepts and translating them into robust experimental procedures. \n\nThis project is moreover greatly strengthened by my PhD work in adhesion, which explored hysteretic effects associated with surface separation among other things. As much of my prior work in adhesion is in computational modeling, Tom’s experimental background will form a nice complement. In fact, I have long since thought of carrying out a study on this topic, but until now I did not have a student with the proper experimental skills in this area. \n\nNot only do I feel that the project is apt given our research backgrounds, but I also am intrigued by its prospects. Until recently, it was not possible to perform a systematic inquiry into the origins of transverse forces in a solid-solid interface. Thus this project has an excellent potential to reshape current frameworks regarding contact mechanics and the origins of friction.\n\nI have reviewed all of Tom’s application materials and they seem to offer a strong proposal overall. Furthermore, I also worked with Tom on generating ideas for the research proposal, so I am familiar with its merits and their caliber.\n\nIt is therefore my great pleasure to recommend Tom for this fellowship whom I believe to be an excellent candidate. \n\n\end{newlfm}\n\end{document}\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n" > ~/Downloads/dummy.tex
